          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1924579908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17755369114815459381">2.5 stars. I unfortunately was not a big fan of Caraval, which is very disappointing to me considering I was really excited for it!<br/><br/>Pretty much, everything about this book fell short for me. Every character was bland and annoying with no personality. The romance had absolutely no substance in my opinion, I never felt any chemistry or understood why they got together other than the fact that they were basically one of the only people available to the other. The setting of Caraval was so much less </span>
  <span id="freeText17755369114815459381" style="display:none">2.5 stars. I unfortunately was not a big fan of Caraval, which is very disappointing to me considering I was really excited for it!<br /><br />Pretty much, everything about this book fell short for me. Every character was bland and annoying with no personality. The romance had absolutely no substance in my opinion, I never felt any chemistry or understood why they got together other than the fact that they were basically one of the only people available to the other. The setting of Caraval was so much less magical and whimsical than I anticipated, and even the darker portions of the performance weren't dark enough! The tagline is "It's all an elaborate performance," but it felt nothing like a performance at all. It felt like one big, wishy-washy scavenger hunt, not the *amazing, adventurous* experience we're lead to believe.<br /><br />The magic system itself really irked me. It felt like a bad case of "This happens because !*~.- m A g I c -.~*!" with very little explanation as to how the magic works. I don't feel there were many limitations, and the restrictions that were present weren't all that clear. The magic system was severely underdeveloped in my opinion, which is a big issue for me as a reader. <br /><br />There definitely were points where I was more interested and entertained by the story (thought those only occurred when I could block out at least a 3 hour uninterrupted period, which is not typical for my audiobook listening) but overall, it was a tough book to get through. I don't often consider putting books down, but there were times when I questioned why I was still listening and contemplated not finishing it.<br /><br />Ultimately, this book felt very juvenile for me (that is not to say books intended for younger readers are not as good!) but I tend to enjoy more mature YA novels. That being said, I can see why there is so much hype for this book, especially within readers younger than myself. I think younger Emma MIGHT have enjoyed it more, considering I don't look at books the same way I did at 17. <br /><br />I'm not sure if I'd read book two, I'd have to see how I feel about this story around the time it comes out. But considering I felt Caraval would have fared better as a standalone, it just doesn't seem like this series is for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17755369114815459381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1616564897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616564897" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616564897?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=annoying-heroine">annoying-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616564897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17778218064438867618">I had really high hopes for <i>Caraval</i>. The blurb, the cover, and the excellent reviews promised a magical whirlwind of a story. And this novel delivered that, but its relatively achieved grandeur was overshadowed bit by bit till the end. The last 50 pages or so of the book took its soul out, leaving me with a bittersweet aftertaste, a headache and lots of confusion. <br/><br/>Since I cannot even reflect upon the messy thoughts inside my brain, I'll analyze punctually. <br/><br/><b>1. The world-building.</b> Sadly, in its tr</span>
  <span id="freeText17778218064438867618" style="display:none">I had really high hopes for <i>Caraval</i>. The blurb, the cover, and the excellent reviews promised a magical whirlwind of a story. And this novel delivered that, but its relatively achieved grandeur was overshadowed bit by bit till the end. The last 50 pages or so of the book took its soul out, leaving me with a bittersweet aftertaste, a headache and lots of confusion. <br><br>Since I cannot even reflect upon the messy thoughts inside my brain, I'll analyze punctually. <br><br><b>1. The world-building.</b> Sadly, in its true meaning and ramifications, we have no such thing as world-building. I do not even know how to categorize this novel. High-fantasy? Just fantasy? Regardless, in the beginning we had mentions of empires and conquered isles which had me utterly excited, but they were left to rot in the backseat so that the world of Caraval could unravel. Moving to this microcosm, it was indeed complex and fascinating. However, only through its captivating appearance and bold imagery and creative ideas. If you dive deeper, into the background, mechanisms and history, you come up empty. It's all really a facade. <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-p8FAygZJ_RI/WJzV_Tgd_yI/AAAAAAAARDo/24vj2LQKKLQ6HHhwAGucAjxVAqyZCGinQCLcB/s1600/913cfa60f75cfce6c4ac7466e200886f.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486673475i/21939934.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>2. The plot.</b> God, the lies. There were so many lies and so many secrets and so many games and manipulation that it honestly ended up being exhausting. Revelations upon revelations, ones that often contradict each other, keep you guessing from start to finish, but after a while this initially mesmerizing stance metamorphoses into the feel of being tricked. Personally, that's how I felt. Deceived. After all the puzzle pieces finally straightforwardly fell into place (some that I've anticipated, some that I did not) you are offered an explanation. And like all good magic tricks, this kills the spirit -- and, implicitly, the so called "plot" -- of Caraval. Gone is the magic and wonder; instead, the triviality and over-the-top drama take residence. It's a scam. A ploy. And, much like Scarlett felt in last key-scenes, I also felt I haven't really made progress in the story. <br><br><b>3. The characters.</b> We have Scarlett, our heroine; Julian, the love-interest; Donatella, the sister. Governor Dragna, the father and also the villain. Legend, the pseudo villain and the mastermind behind Caraval. Plus a few secondary, yet admirable characters (them I liked in their entirety). Scarlett could have been awesome, I'm telling you, if it weren't for her constant fretting and worrying and flowery thinking. Her personality was nuanced only in the kind, moral and brave spectrum, but at least a fraction of character development existed. Julian is a completely other story. The hottie and protective type, he was so intricately woven into the scam I've mentioned that he missed becoming a swoony book boyfriend. Tella was, on the other hand, funky and with a mind of her own, but her supposed cleverness the author tries to sell us falls flat. Despite their flaws, the sisters had a nice relationship. Their father represents a villain-wannabe that should only be called as he truly is -- an abuser, a bully. Legend... now Legend was a mystery and I'd love to find out more. The epilogue seems to hint we'll see him again in a sharper focus. <br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-xvQUp4qtXPU/WJzV_UcTRMI/AAAAAAAARDs/TbRh-ykK78A3VejX2uM0_d-kVKqDzYpIwCLcB/s1600/b8c671305e783af2824e87009c5ef339.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486673476i/21939935.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4. The romance.</b> A bit too syrupy and insta-love reminiscing. I realize now it's the same feeling I've had when reading <i>Falling Kingdoms</i>: it's too much, too early in too little pages. About a quarter into the book, the feelings developed by Scarlett for Julian were already getting in the way of the plot. And I am quite the romantic fan girl, so when I'm saying something felt off, I'm not doing it lightly. Taking into account the amount of untruths that they based their relationship on, it's yet again a case of a shaky foundation to a central aspect of the book. <br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-c9p02zsiOZo/WJzV_fWmFXI/AAAAAAAARDk/NfL1kVeQzcQ83stOJ09Dttt60Syh8IrjACLcB/s1600/b6b6f5b17a1ca2b89c591f84f3d9ba4c.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486673476i/21939936.jpg" width="217" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>5. The writing style.</b> Expect prose the likes of Laini Taylor. It sounds beautiful and I'll admit I get swept away pretty easily with this type of writing. It felt like the story flowed, despite its numerous hiccups. The third-person narrative also helped induce a darker atmosphere to keep us on the edge. On a structural level, there was redundancy, but I managed to overlook it gradually. Overall, I'll keep an eye out for Stephanie Garber, because this debut certifies she has storytelling skills. <br><br>Even though <i>Caraval</i> has been pitched as <i>The Night Circus</i> in different and refreshing clothing, it is far from the lovely and slow-burning tale of Celia and Marco. Nonetheless, I wholeheartedly believe it deserves at least a skimming. It's an enigmatic story from start to finish and the epilogue assured I'll read the sequel. Color me intrigued. <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17778218064438867618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1899590130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1899590130" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1899590130?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1899590130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4751360925844742081"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487817307i/22054113._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This story was so magical, so whimsical, and so perfect.</b> I was skeptical, because I'm pretty much the only person on Goodreads that did not like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454908658' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Night Circus</a>, but this didn't remind me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454908658' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Night Circus</a> at all. Well, at least the 15% I read before I couldn't force myself to read more. I mean, I can see where people would draw the parallels because of the plot, but the writing in this is much more reminiscent of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453987155' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499783627' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heartless</a>. The prose is the epitome of lyrical, with descript</span>
  <span id="freeText4751360925844742081" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487817307i/22054113._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This story was so magical, so whimsical, and so perfect.</b> I was skeptical, because I'm pretty much the only person on Goodreads that did not like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454908658" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>, but this didn't remind me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454908658" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a> at all. Well, at least the 15% I read before I couldn't force myself to read more. I mean, I can see where people would draw the parallels because of the plot, but the writing in this is much more reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453987155" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499783627" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a>. The prose is the epitome of lyrical, with descriptions that were nothing short of magical, and I devoured it all with a smile on my face.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It looked like a storybook come to life. She peered down at bright pointy rooftops, moss-covered towers, gingerbread cottages, gleaming gold bridges, blue-brick streets, and bubbling fountains, all lit by candled lamps that hung everywhere, giving an appearance of time that was neither day nor night.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Can we talk about how this is Stephanie Garber’s debut novel? I am seriously shocked, because this is not the writing of a new or amateur writer. She has perfected her craft, and made just a really addictive and impressive first story. <br><br>God, the writing was so good. The descriptions were perfection. I understand this might not be for everyone, but this world consumed me and I didn't want to leave when I turned the last page. I know this book is about a magical place, but it truly ended up being a magical experience that I'm not going to forget anytime soon. <br><br>The plot of this has a perfect thriller tempo, too! Yes, I've been raving about how magical and lyrical this book is, but I have to emphasize that the pace is fast, too! Each chapter holds a new mystery, and I felt so compelled to never put this book down. <i>Caraval</i> truly is a fast and magical journey that I can't help but recommend everyone take! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486072355ra/21878927.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Caraval</i> is a magical game that is played once a year. Not everyone can go, but the lucky ones are sent tickets, and once they arrive they are able to choose if they'd like to watch the game or actually play the game. Scarlett has been writing to the master of Caraval, Legend, her whole life in hopes to acquire tickets for her and her sister, and after all these years she finally gets a letter back.<br><br>And the sibling love in this is so amazing. My brother and I are really close, and there is nothing I wouldn't do for him. Scarlett's devotion to her sister warmed my heart completely and I loved reading about it. Also, seeing them pick each other over boys is my freaking jam. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482305470ra/21501933.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book also tackles the hard topic of parental abuse, emotional, mental, and physical. This topic is so important, and doesn't seem to be in much YA, unless it is the center of the story. So many kids grow up being abused, yet, it doesn't become the center of their life. Seeing Scarlett realize she is not the value of her father's rage was beautiful. We need more books that handle this issue, because Uncle Vernon and Harry Potter isn't close to being the epitome of an abusive relationship. Many parents can be manipulative, abusive, terrible, and it isn't the victims fault, ever. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People think no one sees all the nasty things they do in the dark. The foul acts they commit, or the lies they tell as part of the game. Caraval takes place at night because you like to watch, and see what people do when they think there are no consequences.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book does border on unreliable narrative though, because as Scarlett is learning the rules of the game and the magic of Caraval, so is the reader. Caraval is a facade, it might be a beautiful facade, but it is still a facade. The reader is never sure if what they are reading is true, and that is because Scarlett never knows if what she is experiencing is true. I loved the mystery factor and thought it worked perfectly, but I can see where others might not like it as much as me. <br><br>And the characters and players in this world are so wonderful! Scarlett was my favorite, and I feel like it would be almost impossible not to fall in love with her. Her sister, Tella, has a good heart and her actions were coming from a good place, but she was a little frustrating. Hopefully, in the next book, my love for Scarlett will carry over to Tella. Julian is the other main character you read about, alongside Scarlett. His character was so endearing and I absolutely loved this story-arc and twist(s). Not knowing whether to root and cheer for him or wish him dead was a unique experience to say the least! <br><br>I loved this book. I loved it with my whole heart. I read this in one day; I couldn't put it down. This book is the definition of a sensory read. Please give it a try. I understand that not every book is for everyone, but this book is pretty close to perfection, in my eyes. I whole heartedly expect this to show up on my "Best of 2017" list, and I cannot wait to get my hands on the sequel. <br><br>I'll be honest, between this book and Beyoncé announcing she's having twins, I feel like the world is trying to ease the blow of Donald Trump's next executive order.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486072305ra/21878913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://steamcommunity.com/id/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Steam</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4751360925844742081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1964607844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1964607844" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1964607844?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=paranormal-and-gothic">paranormal-and-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=period-aus-past">period-aus-past</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1964607844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17802165961632182485"><blockquote>
  <i>Our futures are only predictable because as creatures of this world we are predictable.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>I really did want to like this book. <br/>I really did want to dive into a magical and dark adventure with Scarlett and Tella.<br/><br/>Sadly for me, I didn’t enjoy it the way I thought I would, and this adventure turned out to be a little school trip to Boredom Land, with one heck of a frustrating main character. <br/>And don’t even let me start on her sister.<br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/pyYr' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515090798ra/24832321.gif' alt='tumblr_mo1dpesk3o1sp9fcho1_400.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>The premise is good, though it has its little flaws right from</span>
  <span id="freeText17802165961632182485" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Our futures are only predictable because as creatures of this world we are predictable.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><br>I really did want to like this book. <br>I really did want to dive into a magical and dark adventure with Scarlett and Tella.<br><br>Sadly for me, I didn’t enjoy it the way I thought I would, and this adventure turned out to be a little school trip to Boredom Land, with one heck of a frustrating main character. <br>And don’t even let me start on her sister.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/pyYr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515090798ra/24832321.gif" alt="tumblr_mo1dpesk3o1sp9fcho1_400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>The premise is good, though it has its little flaws right from the start. <br>The writing, for one, has a dull and chanting rhythm. There are a few nice quotes here and there, but nothing remarkable. Dialogues and <s>attempted</s> bantering included.<br>Gosh, those dialogues. *shivers* I’ll have nightmare for days.<br>The characters are infuriatingly undefined. <br>Their personalities and traits are smudgy on their borders. They all read the same way, they all look and talk the same, and they lack of substance, insomuch that, still now, I can’t understand what the deal was with a lot of them.<br>Scarlett is not that bad, but if I had to tip the scale in favor of a concrete judgment, I’d say she’s an easily forgettable character. <br>Sometimes I found myself wanting to jump into the book, grab her by her shoulders and give her a vigorous shake because, holy crow, her obliviousness got on my nerves more times than I can count. <br>She’s really insecure and timorous, yet patsy and judgy to the point of aversion. <br>To an extent, I see how her father’s abuse has a part in all of this. Yet, as someone who’s supposed to be the tough and motherly sister, I feel like she’s way too immature and naïve, too ready to give away her feelings to those who don’t deserve it. <br>Still, I’m not holding any of this against her, because poor Scarlett is basically an unconsciously willing victim of circumstance.<br>Tella, on the other hand…<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/pyZV" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515090797ra/24832320.gif" alt="giphy176af3f2db88f44d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>She's so flipping selfish and dumb. I really hope Scarlett will grow some balls and tell her off. Oh, scratch that, just give her a well deserved noogie. <br>Julian, Mr Love Interest, could not be there and I wouldn’t notice, or wouldn’t care. I probably would have liked him more if he wasn’t always trying so hard. His purposes and aims are so conventionally confined into the “typical mysterious good-looking guy” category, and his flirting is so bland that you can’t even go past the fact that he’s just another pretty face in another unpretty book. <br>I’m not even gonna waste my words on Legend and all the *sarcastic air quotes* mystery that surrounds him. Fuck you, you old fart. Give me my money back.<br><br>Luckily enough, the plot is probably the thing I liked the most, even if I probably hyped this book too much in my own head to the point it took me exactly 270 pages to feel the reader’s high. <br>The setting is gorgeous, I got to give it to the author. Had she wrote about flowers and dresses and a whole another kind of circus-like place (one where, supposedly, Scarlett is a badass and Tella is participating in an Erasmus program in Grunland), I would have fallen hard for it.<br>I wish she’d focused more on describing the surroundings, giving more space and a proper background story to more secondary characters, instead of going on, pages and pages, about feelings and stuff.<br>However, I loved the way everything merges together and gives the story, its performers and the entirety of Caraval, this Venetian, carnivalesque freak-show kind of halo. <br>Alas, things started to get interesting when I was already too far into the book and already too oriented towards a negative outcome, so I probably didn’t even enjoy it as much as I could have.<br><br>I kind of was expecting that ending, to be honest. <br>It’s the kind of book that requires something shocking, that leaves people with their mouth and eyes wide open buuuut...nope, I'm not impressed at all. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17802165961632182485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1850490712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850490712" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1850490712?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30065677-caraval">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850490712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17812153215637960515">What a surprisingly captivating world Stephanie Garber has created in 'Caraval'! I listened to the Audible version of this book and I was mesmerized by the beautiful and vivid imagery that 'Caraval' contained. I was drawn in by the world that Ms. Garber created and it held my attention right to the very end.<br/><br/>Every once in a while, I love a great paranormal romance. I love to leave reality behind and take off on a journey to a place where magic and fairytales exist. This was the perfect story to d</span>
  <span id="freeText17812153215637960515" style="display:none">What a surprisingly captivating world Stephanie Garber has created in 'Caraval'! I listened to the Audible version of this book and I was mesmerized by the beautiful and vivid imagery that 'Caraval' contained. I was drawn in by the world that Ms. Garber created and it held my attention right to the very end.<br /><br />Every once in a while, I love a great paranormal romance. I love to leave reality behind and take off on a journey to a place where magic and fairytales exist. This was the perfect story to do just that.<br /><br />Scarlett, aka "Crimson", and her sister Tella have lived under the oppressive rule of their father. His cruelty seems to know no bounds and he takes satisfaction in tormenting his daughters. Knowing how close the girls are to one another, he uses their love against them. When one of his daughters breaks a rule, it is the other one that will receive the punishment. <br /><br />Awaiting her arranged marriage to a Count that she's never met before, Scarlett is just biding her time until she can get away from her sadistic father. She's literally counting down the weeks until she will be married and can take her sister with her to her new home. Unlike Scarlett, Tella is skeptical of the mysterious fiancé that seems to say all of the right things but whose identity remains shrouded in mystery.<br /><br />Before Scarlett can be married off, she receives an invitation from Legend, the famous mastermind behind the Caraval. Despite writing to Legend ever since she was a young child, Scarlett has never received a response before. Now, with the clock counting down to her wedding, it seems like fate that she would receive her first ever response and an invitation to participate in the Caraval.<br /><br />With the support of her sister, Scarlett sets off for the mysterious island where Legend has indicated that the Caraval is taking place. Along with Tella, she sets sail with Julian, a young sailor, to participate in the forbidden game. Both sisters know that they are risking their lives by sneaking off against their father's wishes. However, they are willing to take their chances in order to seize a once in a lifetime opportunity.<br /><br />From that point forward, the girls are caught up in a magical and dangerous world. Appearances are not what they seem and even time moves differently in this new world. Caraval is a game where the stakes are very high and not everyone will come out alive or unscathed.<br /><br />I don't want to give anything away or ruin the surprise for others. There were many twists and turns that I didn't see coming while listening to this story. Just when I thought I had everything figured out, something else would happen that made me question everything again. This story held my attention and kept me guessing right to the very end.<br /><br />If you like adventure/fantasy/paranormal stories with plenty of twists and turns, this is a great choice. There is some romance, but it took a back seat to the magical world of Caraval. For me, the adventure and mystery of Caraval reigned supreme. Of course, there is a love story weaved into this fantastical story as well. Just, don't plan on a super-smutty type of story where the focus on the romance is paramount.<br /><br />All in all, I thought that this was a wonderful story. I was enchanted by the world that Ms. Garber created and cannot wait to read the next installment. This book filled my head with some beautiful and vibrant imagery that will hang with me for quite some time. I highly recommend this book to anyone looking for a paranormal/fantasy/adventure to read. It was fantastic!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17812153215637960515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2647543198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2647543198" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2647543198?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2647543198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5313841003600291933"><b>It felt like stepping into a world made of dreams and nightmares, laced with the spicy essence of desire and the cloying smell of fear.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>❝ Remember, it's only a game. ❞</i>
</blockquote><br/>Oh, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14137787.Stephanie_Garber' title='Stephanie Garber' rel='nofollow noopener'> Stephanie Garber</a> appears to be an expert at playing games, <b>a master of manipulation and misdirection</b>. My mind is still clouded, drunk in cider, unable to grasp the boundaries between sweet fiction and reality; I was her puppet numerous times, suspicious, disappointed, frustrated when she wanted me to, <b>enamored yet terrified</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5313841003600291933" style="display:none"><b>It felt like stepping into a world made of dreams and nightmares, laced with the spicy essence of desire and the cloying smell of fear.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>❝ Remember, it's only a game. ❞</i>
</blockquote><br>Oh, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14137787.Stephanie_Garber" title="Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Stephanie Garber</a> appears to be an expert at playing games, <b>a master of manipulation and misdirection</b>. My mind is still clouded, drunk in cider, unable to grasp the boundaries between sweet fiction and reality; I was her puppet numerous times, suspicious, disappointed, frustrated when she wanted me to, <b>enamored yet terrified</b>, always complying with her whims. Perhaps that's what makes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a> so <b>seductive</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <i>❝ Every person has the power to change their fate if they are brave enough to fight for what they desire more than anything. ❞</i>
</blockquote><br>Scarlett and Tella. Tella and Scarlett. Two sisters bound by love and fear, two sisters abused by their father, searching for the way out. The chance was presented when a wickedly handsome sailor entered their lives at the same time when Scarlett found in her hands what she craved ever since she was a little child: tickets to Caraval, a week-long show that promised magic. Adventure. <i>Escape</i>. What Scarlett didn't predict, though, was that as soon as she stepped foot on Caraval, her sister would be kidnapped by Legend, the show's master. That her beloved Tella would become a part of the game, and that she would embark on a race against time, accompanied by the rugged sailor that hid dark secrets. That Caraval would blind, confuse, dazzle, ensnare her in its net of murders, deceit, and, well, magic. Scarlett must remember that Caraval is only a game before she loses her soul.<br><blockquote>
  <i>❝ Whatever you've heard about Caraval, it doesn't compare to the reality. It's more than just a game or performance. It's the closest you'll ever find yourself magic in this world.❞</i>
</blockquote><br>At first, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a> was the source of conflicting feelings. While I sensed that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14137787.Stephanie_Garber" title="Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Stephanie Garber</a> was weaving a web of many-coloured yarns ready to trap me, there was one problem: <b>the writing was overwrought</b>, and it remained so for the rest of the book. I usually love whimsical writing, writing brimming with strange yet oddly fitting metaphors, but in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a>'s instance the <b>purple prose</b> of most descriptions somehow dampened my enthusiasm towards an otherwise <b>enchanting</b> read. However, that did not dissuade me from enjoying the story; hunting for clues alongside Scarlett and Julian, bearing witness to marvels and horrors and twisted imagination was my cup of tea afer all.<br><br>For me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a> will forever be associated with <b>warmth</b>. I can't pinpoint whether such warmth is the product of the delicious chemistry between Scarlett and Julian, the dangerous and sweet vibes that emanated from the ambience, the wild abandon of a magical event that unfolded at night, covering in mist sinister deeds and thoughts, or the idea of the show itself; a show where dresses and all kinds of peculiar goods are traded with secrets, dreams and blood. The truth is that whilst reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a> I lost connection with the world around me. I had fallen so deep into its cluches that the ascension back to reality took tremendous effort, like fighting against a current. <br>I ended up <b>mesmerized.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1546703048i/26863650._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://whimsicalpublishing.ca/shop/the-perfect-ending/" rel="nofollow noopener">[Source of this incredible piece of art]</a><br><br>I don't know how I feel towards the characters. They were intriguing, they were flawed, but I didn't actually elaborate on my feelings and impressions of them. They were simply <i>there</i>, a part of something bigger, my guides to a mysterious island and a world I long to discover. In the end, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener"> Caraval</a> <i>was</i> more than a game. <b>It pulsed, it breathed and it devoured me.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5313841003600291933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1758717981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758717981" />
    <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books"><img alt="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464902542p2/372001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1758717981?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books">Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=2017-release">2017-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758717981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195933865654927344">4.5/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href='http://wp.me/s6sNGI-caraval' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dana and the Books</a><br/><br/>I had high expectations <em>and</em> low expectations stepping into <em>Caraval. </em>Everyone who's read it has been gushing over what a masterpiece it is. But then it was also endlessly compared to <em>The Night Circus</em>. Confession: I didn't like <em>The Night Circus</em>, so I was concerned that I just wouldn't be the target reader for <em>Caraval</em>.  Within the first few pages, it was clear that I was going to fawn over it.<br/><br/><p>
  
    <strong>
      <em>"Remember, it's only a g</em></strong></p></span>
  <span id="freeText17195933865654927344" style="display:none">4.5/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://wp.me/s6sNGI-caraval" rel="nofollow noopener">Dana and the Books</a><br /><br />I had high expectations <em>and</em> low expectations stepping into <em>Caraval. </em>Everyone who's read it has been gushing over what a masterpiece it is. But then it was also endlessly compared to <em>The Night Circus</em>. Confession: I didn't like <em>The Night Circus</em>, so I was concerned that I just wouldn't be the target reader for <em>Caraval</em>.  Within the first few pages, it was clear that I was going to fawn over it.<br /><br /><p>
  
    <strong>
      <em>"Remember, it's only a game..."</em>
    </strong>
  
</p><br />Is it just a game? Is any of it real? Like the players, it certainly didn't feel like a game judging by the amount of times my heart rate increased. I loved discovering new clues alongside Scarlett, stumbling into roadblocks, and overcoming seemingly life threatening obstacles. I haven't been swept away in such a carousel of a story in a long time and am delighted I got to experience such an adventure in <em>Caraval</em>.<br /><br />Stephanie Garber is a beautiful writer. Her sentences strung together so fluidly, painting a fitting picture for the Caraval world she created. Scarlett, Tella, and Julian jumped off the pages straight away. She wrote such a strong opener with well developed, three-dimensional characters; I was sucked in immediately and had no choice but to stay up and read until the small hours of the morning.<br /><br />The twists were clever and not too over the top, bringing the final chapter to a satisfying conclusion. I believe there is a sequel planned, but I felt a good deal of closure with the ending as it is (but I am definitely going to be first in line to step back into this world!)<br /><br /><em>Caraval </em>may end up being one of the biggest YA books of 2017. And rightfully so!<br /><br />Thanks so much to Hodder &amp; Stoughton for giving me a copy to review through NetGalley!<br /><br /><br />It's out Jan 31, you don't want to be late! (<a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Caraval-Stephanie-Garber/9781473629141/?a_aid=DanaAndTheBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2k1jNPc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2jG7Z3M" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon Canada</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2jnx0Qh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>)<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17195933865654927344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1905705860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1905705860" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1905705860?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=magic-stuff">magic-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905705860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5128515977333015417"><b>Did anyone else see this while they were reading?</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493993914i/22674325.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So how <i>do</i> you pronounce this, exactly?<br/>In my head, I was saying it like Carnival without the <i>n</i> sound. Well, actually, I ended up trying out a few different pronunciations in my head (see example above), and eventually settled on that one...ish. Because, and I don't know if I'm the only one who does this or what, I've noticed that I kind of mumble stuff that I'm not 100% sure how to say. <br/>Yes. In my head. I'll mumble shit in my head.<br/>And you know what</span>
  <span id="freeText5128515977333015417" style="display:none"><b>Did anyone else see this while they were reading?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493993914i/22674325.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So how <i>do</i> you pronounce this, exactly?<br>In my head, I was saying it like Carnival without the <i>n</i> sound. Well, actually, I ended up trying out a few different pronunciations in my head (see example above), and eventually settled on that one...ish. Because, and I don't know if I'm the only one who does this or what, I've noticed that I kind of mumble stuff that I'm not 100% sure how to say. <br>Yes. In my head. I'll mumble shit in my head.<br>And you know what? It doesn't really matter, I was just curious.<br><b>Moving on!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493992885ra/22674265.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, this was fun. I'm not one of the screaming/crying fangirls of this thing, but it <i>was</i> a <b>really</b> cool little book.<br>The premise is complicated, but in a good way. <br>Scarlett and Tella are sisters living with an extremely abusive father. Tella is the wild child, while Scarlett is the proper one who tries to do the right thing. Both sisters are devoted to each other, though.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493997718ra/22674698.gif" width="400" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright, Scarlett's relationship with Tella, and the stuff with their father is what initially drew me into the story. A couple pages and <b>Bam!</b> I'm sucked in, couldn't stop reading!<br>But then the book takes off in a different direction, and there's also all the weird stuff about some sort of a magic traveling carnival, and some equally odd backstory about the guy who runs it. It was kinda confusing, especially at first!<br>Like, there doesn't seem to be magic in their world, but <i>this</i> place is magic? And then there's the whole <i>game</i> aspect to it.<br>I mean, is she at a magical state fair, or is she a contestant on some sort of Alice In Wonderland game show?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493997718ra/22674699.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's purposely vague for a reason, though. There are all these little layers of mystery to the story, and it wouldn't work very well if it were spelled out to either the reader or Scarlett.<br>But the bottom line is that she's got 5 nights to win a game with ambiguous rules in order to supposedly save her sister. Maybe. Because who knows how much of the game is real?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493997718ra/22674700.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Toss in a sexy sailor with mysterious reasons for helping her, a possible vendetta against her family played out during the game, being stalked by her sadistic father, and a wedding to the man of her <s>hopefully</s> dreams only a few days away? <br>Well, it makes for a pretty interesting ride.<br>The ending is nice and tidy, but there's also a teaser at the end that makes me want to see where this story is going. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493997718ra/22674701.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not normally a fan of trippy stories like this, but this one was an exception. Very different.<br>And I mean that in a good way. <br><b>Recommended!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5128515977333015417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1795924467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795924467" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795924467?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=savage-review">savage-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=literal-trash">literal-trash</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795924467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9408332335153149754"><b>TRIGGER WARNING</b>: this one slipped my attention while reading, purely because I was <i>bored</i>, but I feel it is important to add that this book features parent x child abuse which isn't dealt with. <br/><br/><b>WARNING</b>: this review will be a rant, there may be unmarked spoilers. This is also a highly unpopular opinion so if you want to come at me telling me I'm wrong or didn't understand the book I will punch you in the nose from how mad this book made me. Also, there is a high amount of swearing, which I usually</span>
  <span id="freeText9408332335153149754" style="display:none"><b>TRIGGER WARNING</b>: this one slipped my attention while reading, purely because I was <i>bored</i>, but I feel it is important to add that this book features parent x child abuse which isn't dealt with. <br><br><b>WARNING</b>: this review will be a rant, there may be unmarked spoilers. This is also a highly unpopular opinion so if you want to come at me telling me I'm wrong or didn't understand the book I will punch you in the nose from how mad this book made me. Also, there is a high amount of swearing, which I usually don't try to put in my reviews but I am so angry. (:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Whatever you’ve heard about Caraval, it doesn’t compare to the reality. It’s more than just a game or a performance. It’s the closest you’ll ever find to magic in this world."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Caraval</i> was a book I knew I'd hate, I wasn't even excited for it. Then shallow me saw the inside cover and <i>had</i> to read it. Even after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779481082" rel="nofollow noopener">Caitlin</a>, who I share similar opinions with, was disappointed. Even after it was repeatedly compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>, which I also hated. So, big <b>fuck you</b> to shallow Amber for making me <b>waste</b> my time. <br><br>If you haven't read the book and didn't adhere to my warning at the top of this review, I highly recommend you skedaddle because I am about to go into the characters. So, <b>bye</b>, come back if you hate this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486854219ra/21956125.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For a book where the only review I saw that wasn't a five was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779481082" rel="nofollow noopener">Caitlin's</a>, the character's were so <b>dumb</b> and <b>one-dimensional</b>. They literally had to state everything that was happening. It was infuriating to read after the ridiculous description we had had to read of almost every item. This book would have been <b> a lot shorter</b> without the unnecessary metaphors for <u>everything</u>. It was tiring. <br><br>But, <i>anyway</i>, let's talk about this <b>shit storm</b> of characters. <br><br>First, we have the <b>dumb ass</b>, <b>possible whore</b>(not slut shaming just stating it could be a fact), and <b>ninja turtle</b> of a sister. Now, you may be like, 'where did the ninja turtle part come from?' Well, my friends, her name is <b>Donatella</b>. <br><br>So, how did I picture this dimwitted sister the whole time?<br><br>Much like <b>this</b>:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486854219ra/21956126.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A giant turtle with a purple eye band. <br><br>Then add this gif - because for some reason we were meant to think that Julian and Ninja Turtle had hooked up. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486854797ra/21956263.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moving on, we have the <b>oh so romantic</b> kidnapper known as Julian. Now, you may be like '<i>woah, a kidnapper?! Are we meant to like him?!</i>' Don't worry, his brown muscles will distract from that. Nothing else matters because he has brown muscles and a solid chest. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486854219i/21956127._SY540_.png" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Have you forgotten he kidnapped the main character (who I am looking forward to <b>shitting on</b> next)? Me neither. The fact he <b>never</b> called Scarlett by her real name, favouring "Crimson" instead, really irked me. She corrected him <b>once</b> and left it. I've had people call me Amanda for a year, and I corrected them every single time, so it irked me that Scarlett was that weak of a character she wouldn't stand up for herself. <br><br>Now, let's talk about <b>Scarlett</b>. Honestly, the most dim-witted character I have <b>ever</b> read. She was so <b>stupid</b> that it made this book a struggle. Her absolute inability to do anything correctly, the fact she couldn't solve the clues and the fact she was so hopelessly okay with almost everything was <b>infuriating</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453398637ra/17822510.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, you may be waiting for a representation of Scarlett. I got nothing. I basically pictured her as an 'attractive' blob on legs. Oops. Add that to a blushing virgin and you have Scarlett, the girl who could barely look a male character in the eye. <br><br><b>The plot</b> was even <b>worse</b>. When you have a book with the preface of "it's all a game" and "nothing is real", it's going to be fucking boring when you try to add 6385923759 plot twists at the end that are <b>dumbdumb</b>. Everything about it had me spluttering in anger and sending <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779481082" rel="nofollow noopener">Caitlin</a> 80 billion messages. <br><br>Honestly, I can't even begin to express my utter <b>anger</b> and <b>hatred</b> for this book. It is <b>literally</b> told over a week and somehow there's a fucking love story too. Don't even get me started on that shit. My notes for it are just: "this is so fucking DUMB" - exact copy and paste from my notes. <br><br>Ugh, I am still so angry about this book, I don't even want to see it if I can't kick it 169238048 kilometres away from me. I also don't even want to get into the <i>Legend</i> shit that happened or the "oh no you've been fooled" or whatever the fuck happened.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486854797ra/21956264.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To make this even better, I just went through my friends ratings and I've rated it the lowest. So, <b>here's for an unpopular opinion</b>. I mean, I didn't even buy into the hype, how am I this disappointed?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9408332335153149754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1784757816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784757816" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784757816?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784757816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5474042710342495203"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Remember, it’s only a game…</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>I wish you had told me it’s a boring one though, that is.</b><br/><br/>If you were to tell me that I would end up reading Caraval after having it on my tbr for 2 years, I would not have believed you. I remember being suuuuuuper excited for this but never got around to reading it because I simply, truthfully, did not want to spend my money on it after seeing so many mixed reviews, so I waited until my library had it. Now, <i>Legendary</i> is out and my library also has that one </span>
  <span id="freeText5474042710342495203" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Remember, it’s only a game…</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>I wish you had told me it’s a boring one though, that is.</b><br /><br />If you were to tell me that I would end up reading Caraval after having it on my tbr for 2 years, I would not have believed you. I remember being suuuuuuper excited for this but never got around to reading it because I simply, truthfully, did not want to spend my money on it after seeing so many mixed reviews, so I waited until my library had it. Now, <i>Legendary</i> is out and my library also has that one but here I am, reading other books I had never heard of before.<br /><br /><i>Caraval</i> is a manipulative game that two sisters have wished to attend, Scarlett and Donatella Dragna. They have been living on a tiny island they have never left because their cruel, abusive and controlling father who has set a marriage for Scarlett with a man she has never met but sees as charming and a gentleman. When she does not receive a letter back from Legend, the Master of Caraval, she thinks her dreams of attending Caraval are over, but they return when she receives an invitation by the master of Caraval, Legend himself. Scarlett believes taking the risk is not worth taking, but it isn't until a mysterious sailor takes the two sisters into this once in a year performance where the audience either participates or watches the performers. But when the two arrive, Tella is suddenly kidnapped and it's up to Scarlett to find her until the show is over in 5 days. With the help of the mysterious sailor, Julian, Scarlett needs to find Tella in order to become the winner of the show in order for her sister to be safe and back instead of disappearing forever.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Hope is a powerful thing. Some say it’s a different breed of magic altogether. Elusive, difficult to hold on to. But not much is needed.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Trigger/content warning</b> for parent x child abuse and kidnapping.<br /><br />Let's just let the most important thing out: <b>Caraval was not enjoyable since the start.</b> Nothing was intriguing in any way, the writing was not <i>whimsical and beautiful</i>, it was literally like any other YA fantasy. I get this is a debut novel, but damn some debut authors and their debut novels are truly fantastic and just keep your eyes glued to the pages because of how good every page is. <b>In this case, the writing was confusing.</b> If you look at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617129376?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily May's review</a>, you can see why. There's a lot of similies, things being compared, but it fails to be convincing. They're rather, confusing, leaving the reader wondering what the fuck the line actually means. I mean, how do you know what darkness tastes like? And how do you know what acid tastes like? It was 2017 when this was written, so did I miss some sort of science experiment where acid was tasted and the volunteer didn't die? Someone, please tell me what midnight tastes like as well because apparently, Scarlett knows Julian tastes like that. Also, was it him, or his fingers? <br /><br />There were so many times I was confused as to where the plot was going because it seemed like it was taking another turn, but maybe I missed the point at the fact that everything in Caraval is a game and nothing is true or maybe I missed the fact that everything was a lie. Hmm, maybe it was that.<br /><br />Look, everything was full of lies, manipulations, betrayals, and repetitive dialogue that made me hate every character and roll my eyes at them because of how stupid they were. I mean, Scarlett really fell in love with Julian even though he kidnapped her without her even knowing; Tella suddenly disappeared before Scarlett arrived; Julian lied to Scarlett repeatedly but she kept forgiving him because she was so in love with him; Tella was super super super super blind about "Legend" and couldn't believe Scarlett; Scarlett was truly idiotic on the love Tella had for her; everything was truly dumb in this. <br /><br />This is marked as romance, but damn, <b>where is the romance?</b> The <i>romance</i> in this is gross, insta lovey and predictable. I mean, there were no actual kisses on the lips but there were some...<i>on the fingers??</i> Julian is the main interest and got to Scarlett super close this one time and so she got like super hot and licked his fingers and basically felt super hot about it that she wanted nothing more but to feel him and everything was just uncomfortable. There were times when the words "she wanted to kiss him again" were said over and over but there was not one time they actually kissed except for that time. I can't believe Tella and Julian were making the fuck out in the beginning but were never actually boyfriend and girlfriend and then Scarlett and Julian become a thing in the end and such and wow I just hate that, its gross. I was honestly grossed out every time the romance happened. I wish there was none because even though I'm a YA romance fan, sometimes, on unneeded times, it just shouldn't be there. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Every person has the power to change their fate if they are brave enough to fight for what they desire more than anything.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Also, this is like a once in a lifetime thing, but for the like, first time in quite a long time, I didn't like the main male character. This is new because usually, I do, no matter the situations, but I couldn't get into Julian. Scarlett mentioned his broad chest and nice skin color and oh <i>so good looking</i> face to many times that the repetitive descriptions made me feel bad for Julian even because Scarlett checked him out so many times. Like damn, Scarlett was truly horny for him. But in general, I didn't like him because of everything he did, from the kidnapping to the lying, it was all a mess. No wait, <b>HE was a mess.</b><br /><br />But then, of course, everything was a lie and of course, Scarlett was stupid and blind that she forgave him no matter what because <i>oh</i> she was so in love with him.<br /><br />When I went into this, I truly wanted to feel the ride of Caraval, but I couldn't. The atmosphere and world-building was not experienced. The first time I heard about this, I wanted to feel the ride of the ride. Caraval was not experienced in any way. I didn't imagine myself in the dress shop or the islands being told I have tickets and lives left in order to experience this <i>whimsical and poignant</i> yet divine ride. <br /><br />At this point, I don't even know if I want to read the other 2 books. One of my classmates also recommended this book to me and told me she loved it but one thing I've noticed is that we actually have different opinions and thoughts on books. I seem to not take her recommendations seriously because every book she's loved I've ended up hating or not liking at all. I seem to have missed the big point on this point I guess since I've been on the unpopular opinion side lately.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Whatever you've heard about Caraval, it doesn't compare to the reality. It's more than just a game or performance. It's the closest you'll ever find to magic in this world.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Or so, I thought.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5474042710342495203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2006596470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2006596470" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2006596470?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2006596470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11070425447668614122">Scarlett has been writing letters to Legend for years, hoping to see Caraval, a show whose magic she can't even begin to imagine. Scarlett's grandmother told her stories about Legend coming to their island and the life changing show he put on, but Legend doesn't go anywhere twice, and after an accident at one of his shows he stops doing shows for the public. Scarlett and her sister Tella have never left their home island and so seeing Caraval is just a dream for Scarlett. Her last letter to Lege</span>
  <span id="freeText11070425447668614122" style="display:none">Scarlett has been writing letters to Legend for years, hoping to see Caraval, a show whose magic she can't even begin to imagine. Scarlett's grandmother told her stories about Legend coming to their island and the life changing show he put on, but Legend doesn't go anywhere twice, and after an accident at one of his shows he stops doing shows for the public. Scarlett and her sister Tella have never left their home island and so seeing Caraval is just a dream for Scarlett. Her last letter to Legend is written around the time of her impending marriage and surprisingly this time she receives an answer. Yet Scarlett doesn't know how her and Tella can manage to get off the island to go to Caraval without their abusive father's wrath coming down on them. Tella meanwhile is plotting a way to escape from their father with a sailor's, Julian, help when she finds out about the tickets and becomes set on bringing Scarlett off the island with her. <br /><br />I was pretty into the book until about three fourth of the way through. The writing wasn't too bad and I liked the fantasy aspect plus all the action. I was very much into Julian also and he and Scarlett were pretty cute. I just think that the explanation at the end didn't work for me at all. The way things ended up playing out and all the coincidences that piled up through out the book just made it feel messy and not at all well thought out. I was enjoying the idea that everything is a game and the questioning of reality aspect but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when her father showed up with her fiance I started to feel incredulous and then the whole thing with their grandma and Legend and then the fact that Tella planned the whole thing  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> all seemed like too much. It didn't seem like all that convoluted back story was necessary to make the book work and it just ruined it for me. Also the explanation for things was pretty iffy and so I just felt turned off by the time I finished. It started off strong but it lost me there towards the end as things got more and more complicated without reason.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11070425447668614122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1626037276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626037276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16529240302382743520">4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>VIDEO REVIEW: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aPwq5MZ97Os'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aPwq5...</a><br/><br/>Wow. <br/><br/>I have been seeing this book being praised for months now and finally, I understand where the hype is coming from. Magical and whimsical. This story just flies by and I loved getting deeper into it as the storyline progressed. I'm shocked at the fact Stephanie Garber is a debut author and this is only her first book because it was everything I wanted and more. I CANNOT wait for more from this author because my goodness this is</span>
  <span id="freeText16529240302382743520" style="display:none">4.5/5 stars<br /><br />VIDEO REVIEW: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aPwq5MZ97Os">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aPwq5...</a><br /><br />Wow. <br /><br />I have been seeing this book being praised for months now and finally, I understand where the hype is coming from. Magical and whimsical. This story just flies by and I loved getting deeper into it as the storyline progressed. I'm shocked at the fact Stephanie Garber is a debut author and this is only her first book because it was everything I wanted and more. I CANNOT wait for more from this author because my goodness this is only her first book and I'm already anticipating anything else she comes out with.<br /><br />SO happy to say the hype was real for me. <br /><br />If you can't tell I'm trying not to give too much away just because I feel like the less you know the better. This book does a great job at grabbing your attention and taking you through this wonderful book!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ut+xDmn5f/bhXEr0uFSP+RlUmBi457mhmZYXFDIsSYPpGbwUhzP1Rc8gjk7X3IlsUma1b3wEWXzuav76HIqmrg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8bddGNkn3wwz22dNWTu2H+bCjKOldVnuQ1eZ9XcJt/6icVACN+1Vvx2no/c2s7CKrfCh1GGWuTM0q3AbWa9Y0w==')})
  }
//]]>
